class=\"count\"></span><pre class=\"text\"></pre></div>"],"text":["When Coin Weights Vary: Altering coin biases increases the model's sensitivity to each flip, as mismatches between expected and actual flip outcomes significantly affect inferences.\n\nWhen Switching Probabilities Vary: Alterations in the switching probabilities within the parsing model can lead to an overestimation or underestimation of the frequency at which the type of coin being flipped is changed.","The model's parameters, designed to detect variations, can lead to overfitting on random data, causing it to incorrectly identify non-existent patterns. When applying a model with specific parameters to sequences generated by a fair coin, the model may falsely identify patterns due to its sensitivity to random underlying processes.","Basically match, but models will be more sensitive to new data than humans, who are relatively less prone to changing current perceptions","Parameter settings that make the parsing task intrinsically harder for an ideal Bayesian agent are when coin weights are nearly equal (close to 0.5 for both coins) and switching probabilities are close to 0.5. In such cases, distinguishing between the two coins is challenging due to minimal biases and unpredictable switching behavior, leading to increased difficulty. Conversely, settings with more distinct biases and infrequent switches make the task easier as patterns are more pronounced.","Long-Range Dependencies: HMMs may perform poorly when the sequence has dependencies beyond the immediate previous state. Enhancing the model to capture longer history, such as increasing the order of the Markov model or integrating techniques like LSTM networks, can address this issue.\n\nComplex State Dependencies: If the transitions between states are complex or nonlinear, HMMs' simple transition dynamics might be inadequate. Adopting more flexible models for state transitions, like Bayesian net",""],"savedAt":"11/17/2023 11:54:19 PM"}
